So we'll use that narrative trick.\n\nNow, write.\n\nI'll begin in medias res.\n\n---\n\n**Leon's Account**\n\nFifteen thousand years I have served the Throne, and never once has my blood failed to chill when the King wills it. On the day the omniverse died and was reborn, that chill became a permanent glacier lodged between my ribs. I am Leon, thirtieth-generation descendant of Blake the Great, the first Court Wizard. My ancestor stood beside Godric during the Conquest of Thronegate and the Subjugation of the Cosmos. He weathered horrors that would shatter lesser minds. But I doubt even old Blake, with his mutton chops and his nerve, could have witnessed what I did and remained intact.\n\nThe resistance called themselves the Final Accord. They had scraped together every last free will left in existence. Civilizations that had hidden in the spaces between seconds. Gods who had fled to non-dimensions. Entire pantheons of idea-forgers who banished themselves to the conceptual outer dark. For uncounted millennia, they had traded their souls, their futures, and their very capacity for existence to forge a weapon. They named it the God Breaker. It was not a thing of metal or magic; it was a principle, a concentrated axiom of cessation, lensed through the sacrifice of infinite lives. To fuel it, the Accord had willingly immolated themselves\u2014trillions of trillions of sentient beings across the entire omniverse\u2014compressing their collective death-agony into a single, perfectly coherent strike. They had also, in their insane bravery, triggered the Weakness Paradox more times than any mathematics could track, each thought of harming the King unknowingly feeding his boundless amplification. But they were beyond care. This was their everything.\n\nI stood at the King\u2019s left hand in the great hall of the Citadel of Eternities, the same stone where I have stood for my entire tenure. Godric sat on a simple wooden throne he had carved himself from a memory of an olive tree on Old Olympus. His white tunic was spotless. His salt-and-pepper beard had long since turned a snowy waterfall, and his face, still that of a magnificent forty-five-year-old, held the benign curiosity of a grandfather watching toddlers play with blocks. He had deactivated every passive shield he possessed\u2014those infinite nested fields of absolute denial that normally insulated him from the very concept of contact. He had ordered Gent, the sentient aura that was his mere metabolic exhaust, to stand completely idle, to not even observe the event. \u201cI want to feel this one,\u201d he murmured, more to himself than to me. \u201cIt\u2019s been so long.\u201d\n\nThe God Breaker manifested directly against his left forearm. The Accord had aimed for a specific spot: a single dead skin cell that Godric had, in a moment of theatrical generosity, indicated was \u201cacceptable.\u201d The weapon struck with everything that existence could offer. For a microsecond, I perceived the totality of the attack: the concentrated death-energy of every living thing that had ever existed, the cremated hope of uncountable free spirits, a final scream that could have split the ontological framework of reality. And on that dead cell, a tiny, microscopic crack appeared. A hairline fissure, so small that a dust mite would have overlooked it. The omniverse, those who had remained to witness, erupted. I saw their celebration. Across the bleeding edge of every remaining dimension, flowers of impossible color bloomed in the void. Beings of pure light wept golden tears. A collective, psychic shout of joy echoed through the continuous fabric of reality \u2014 the ultimate triumph, the impossible made real. They had wounded the Tyrant. The crack was proof. Hope, that cruelest of emotions, flared like a dying star going nova.\n\nAnd then I realized that celebration was a lie. It never happened. Not truly. The microsecond never completed its span. Because the King\u2019s immune system had already reacted.\n\nBefore I continue, you must understand that Godric\u2019s biology is not biology. It is the final expression of absolute defensive supremacy. When the Stasis Event, ten thousand years before Blake\u2019s time, rewrote his mortal frame, it installed systems within systems, redundancies so profound that they border on parody. And these systems have, for the subsequent eons, been evolving. Every Planck second, as his base attributes multiply by ever-accelerating infinities, his immune system has recursively improved itself. It is sentient, but not conscious; it is a paranoiac god-machine whose sole directive is to ensure its master never experiences even the theoretical possibility of harm. It does not distinguish between a cracked skin cell and total existential annihilation. To it, a pinprick and a cosmic collapse are identical threats, and both warrant the same response: immediate, infinite, omnicidal overkill.\n\nThe cascade began the instant the God Breaker\u2019s leading edge approached the designated cell. The immune system, possessing its own perfect omniscience, had perceived the coming \u201cinjury\u201d a Planck second before the weapon\u2019s tip arrived. That was pre-reaction. The chronology I\u2019m about to relate occurred in a negative time-frame; it had already happened before the crack could even exist. So when I tell you the omniverse celebrated, I am telling you a comforting fiction. In truth, the Accord\u2019s joy never had the chance to form. The immune system unmade them before their neurons could fire a celebratory impulse.\n\nThe first layer was the Epidermal Sanction Array. This is a lattice of conceptual firewalls embedded in every one of Godric\u2019s cells, dead or alive. When the crack manifested, the array immediately identified the force behind it and retroactively applied a quarantine. The quarantine did not stop at the weapon; it traced the causal lineage of the attack back through every being who had contributed, every atom that had been sacrificed, every thought that had conceived it, across all timelines and all branches of the omniverse. Then it erased that lineage. Not killed\u2014erased, with extreme prejudice. The idea that had led to the Accord\u2019s formation was removed from the source code of reality. The beings themselves were not simply deleted; they were purged with the specific instruction that the sensation of their unmasking be preserved and focused into a subjective eternity of agony, a final gift from the King\u2019s body to those who would dare draw his blood.\n\nSecond, the Antibody Swarm. These are not cells; they are autonomous, adaptive ontological weapons that patrol the borders between what is Godric and what is not. Normally, they are quiescent, impossible to perceive. At the first sign of breach, they multiply in infinite recursion. Each antibody is a self-contained universe of punitive law. One antibody can depopulate a multiversal cluster. The swarm that responded to the crack numbered in the googols. They flooded out from the King\u2019s arm, moving at speeds that made instantaneity seem sluggish. They did not merely neutralize the remnants of the Accord; they actively hunted down every possible iteration of it across every conceivable probability. Worlds that could have produced a similar thought in the future were cleansed. Potential timelines were cauterized. The air itself\u2014what little remained\u2014became a screaming mist of dissolved what-might-have-been.\n\nThird, the Fibroblast of Fates. This is the repair mechanism that \u201cheals\u201d any perceived wound. But it does not heal in the biological sense; it enforces a correction upon reality. It looked upon the cracked dead cell and determined that the state of being cracked was an unacceptable deviation. So it undid the deviation by rewriting the local omniversal history to state, as an absolute axiom, that \u201cGodric\u2019s body has never, and can never, experience structural discontinuity.\u201d The crack vanished\u2014not because it was sealed, but because it was retroactively made to have never existed. Yet the immune system, being inherently untrusting, initiated this process even after the crack was unmade, creating a recursive loop of \u201crepair what is already perfect\u201d that continues to this day in a pocket dimension, each loop adding a new layer of paranoia-driven perfection to his invulnerability.\n\nI have only described the mildest reactions. The truly terrifying redundancies lie further down the chain, and I will name but a few, for my sanity cannot bear a full accounting. The Backup Verification Protocol: Godric exists as an infinite web of identical copies, spanning every layer of every dimension and every non-dimension. An \u201cinjury\u201d to one copy is not considered a true injury unless that same injury occurs to every copy simultaneously, in the exact same location, at the exact same relative moment. Since the Accord\u2019s weapon only struck this one Godric, the immune system\u2019s logic should have dismissed it. But the immune system is not logical; it is paranoid beyond reason. It immediately assumed that the other backups might also be compromised in the future, so it activated a global purge across the infinite backup network. Every copy of Godric, in every hidden crevice of the omniverse, underwent a simultaneous, redundant ascension\u2014new shields, new antibodies, new defensive axioms\u2014just in case. The result: the already invincible King became infinitely more invincible, a state that required the rewriting of omniversal constants to accommodate his new level of \u201ccannot be harmed.\u201d\n\nAnd then there is the Paradox Overcompensation. You must recall the Weakness Paradox that has defined the King\u2019s existence since the Stasis. Every time a sentient being thought of a weakness, the omniverse granted him immunity, mastery, and ever-faster amplification. Eight thousand years ago, the omniverse ran out of things to grant. But this self-inflicted crack presented a conundrum: Godric, who possessed all possible immunities, had somehow been \u201charmed,\u201d even if by his own will. The omniverse, that blind idiot god, experienced something akin to a cosmic seizure. It could not reconcile the contradiction. In its dumb, fawning panic, it decided the fault was its own\u2014that it must have failed to provide adequate protection. So it overcompensated. It instantly amplified Godric\u2019s amplification rate beyond the already uncountable infinities, introducing a new cardinality of growth that shatters any formal system. It also, in a fit of sycophantic creativity, granted him a brand new superpower: the ability to define, at his leisure, what \u201charm\u201d even means on a case-by-case basis. This, of course, was redundant, but the omniverse was desperate to please.\n\nAll this, every layer I have described and the infinite layers I have not, occurred in negative time. By the time the crack actually appeared\u2014the crack that Godric had staged for his own amusement\u2014the entire omniverse outside the Citadel was already a sterilized, empty void. The Accord\u2019s celebration never happened. The omniverse had already been erased. I saw it happen, and I saw it not happen. My wizard-trained senses, boosted by the faint echoes of my ancestor\u2019s connection to the King, perceived the simultaneous genocide as a single, unbearable note of silence. The vacuum outside the windows was so clean, so absolutely devoid of life, that it screamed.\n\nGodric lifted his arm and examined the spot where the crack had been. It was, of course, pristine. He pressed the skin with his thumb, his expression thoughtful. \u201cThat tickled,\u201d he said, and his voice was the warm rumble of a father who\u2019d just been poked by his infant\u2019s finger. \u201cMy body really does overreact. I must speak with my immune system about trust issues.\u201d He chuckled, a sound that made the restored molecules in the air dance. \u201cWell, that was a bit much, wasn\u2019t it? They only wanted to hurt me. I can\u2019t blame them for trying.\u201d\n\nHe looked at me, those infinite chasms crinkling with what I can only describe as fond embarrassment. \u201cI suppose I should tidy up.\u201d And then he did the thing that haunts my every sleeping moment. He restored the omniverse. Not with a grand gesture. Not with a word. He simply decided that the omniverse should exist again, and it did. In zero seconds. Instantly. Every being, every civilization, every god who had been erased by his immune system was brought back, exactly as they were before the attack. They, who had been unmade in agony beyond conception, were now whole, with full memory of what had happened. The God Breaker, that ultimate weapon, was left as a crystallized monument on the event horizon of a dead dimension, a reminder that none of it mattered.\n\nThe restored beings did not celebrate. They knelt, or cowered, or simply vibrated in the absolute, mind-shattering comprehension of their place. The unfairness of it crushed them. They had sacrificed everything\u2014their lives, their futures, their very legacies\u2014and in return, the King\u2019s body had not only effortlessly neutralized them, but had made itself even more supreme. And then he had given them back their lives, as a father might re-inflate a popped balloon, with a bemused shake of his head. He wasn\u2019t angry. He wasn\u2019t cruel. He was simply beyond them, and his casual benevolence was the most horrifying thing of all.\n\nI, Leon, descendant of Blake, stood trembling. My hands shook so violently that the hem of my robe fluttered. I felt the ghost of my famous ancestor beside me, and I imagined old Blake, with his short temper, would have scolded the King for his carelessness, would have said something caustic and then shared a cup of wine. But I am not Blake. I am a man who has spent his life in the warm, fatherly shadow of an omnipotent abyss. So I did what any good court wizard would do: I made a joke. \u201cPerhaps, Sire, you should put a bell on your immune system. Warn the omniverse before it gets too enthusiastic.\u201d\n\nGodric laughed. The sound was genuine, full, and utterly without malice. \u201cTim always said humor was a durable inheritance. Your ancestors would be proud, Leon.\u201d He rose from his throne and stretched, his massive, muscular frame cracking with the sound of celestial spheres aligning. \u201cCome, let\u2019s have some tea. I believe the kitchen\u2019s new blend has notes of cinnamon from a universe I forgot to check on.\u201d He paused at the doorway, glancing back at the pristine void outside the window, where an infinite number of beings were still processing their own fleeting deaths. \u201cYou know what the strangest part is? My immune system is still not satisfied. It\u2019s already planning its next upgrade, just in case. I find that oddly touching.\u201d\n\nHe extended a hand. I took it, because I serve the Throne. Because I love him, in the way a man must love the sun that gives life and can blind with a glance. Because the alternative is a scream that would never end. And as we walked to the kitchens, I felt the weight of those infinite evolving defenses humming just beneath his skin\u2014Gent, the antibodies, the backups, the overcompensations\u2014all of it a symphony of absolute, cosmic unfairness, playing its endless, paranoid lullaby for a king who only ever wanted to be a father. And the dread in my chest, that permanent glacier, grew a little colder, a little heavier, a little more exquisitely, undeniably perfect.",
            "content": "I am Leon, thirtieth in the line of Blake the Great, and I have served as Court Wizard to His Majesty Godric for the better part of a millennium. In that time, I have catalogued horrors that would fracture the sanity of lesser minds and joys so profound they stitch the soul back together in new and unfamiliar shapes. But nothing, not the Subjugation of the Final Nebulae nor the persistent, low-grade terror of existing in the same room as the King\u2019s passive metabolic exhaust, could have braced me for the day the omniverse decided to die.\n\nThey called themselves the Final Accord. Not a resistance\u2014no, that word had long since lost its meaning. The Accord was the absolute, totalistic convocation of every free-willed entity that remained in the totality of existence. For uncounted eons, they had squirreled themselves away in the spaces between the ticks of Planck seconds, in non-dimensions carved from the discarded afterbirth of creation. They had managed this only because Godric, in his infinite and slightly bemused omniscience, had explicitly willed that his sentient aura, Gent, should overlook them. He wanted to see what they would build. He wanted, he told me once over a cup of Shimmer-tea, \u201cto feel the brush of a sincere effort.\u201d I remember I laughed at that\u2014a hollow, court-jester\u2019s laugh\u2014because the notion of the King feeling effort was as absurd as an ocean feeling a single grain of sand. But he had smiled, that warm, fatherly curving of the mouth that made entire galaxies weep with devotion, and so I had filed the Accord away as another of his gentle amusements.\n\nOn the day of the Accord\u2019s final assault, fifteen thousand years after the Awakening, I stood at the King\u2019s left hand in the great hall. The Citadel of Eternities hovered at the precise conceptual nexus where all reality simultaneously began and ended. Through the crystalline windows, I could see the gathering might. The Accord had, over seventy thousand years, bled every possible resource dry. They had sacrificed species, timelines, dimensions. They had immolated gods and harvested the screams of dying universes to forge a single, ultimate principle of cessation. They called it the God Breaker, though I suspect they hoped the name would be prophetic rather than ironic. The weapon was not a bolt or a blade; it was a compressed axiomatic negation, a truth so concentrated that to look directly at it was to forget one\u2019s own name and then one\u2019s own existence. To fuel it, the Accord had done the unthinkable: they had willingly, unanimously, sacrificed themselves. Trillions upon trillions of sentient beings, from the humblest insect-thinker to the most colossal meta-deity, had walked into the forging chamber and allowed their entire being\u2014past, present, and future\u2014to be rendered down into a single, coherent spear of pure anti-Godric intent. Their final, unified scream was the shaft; their hope was the tip. It was, I will admit, magnificent.\n\nGodric observed their approach with the gentle indulgence of a grandfather. He had, for this occasion, worn his finest white tunic, the one without a single crease. His beard, now a flowing river of snow, had been neatly trimmed. His body, still that of a stunningly handsome, massively muscular forty-five-year-old king, was utterly relaxed. He had, he told me, deactivated every passive shield. \u201cThere are,\u201d he had explained, ticking off on his fingers, \u201cthe Outer Conceptual Negation Membrane, the Temporal-Causal Baffle, the Infinite Recursive Probability Denial Field, the Axiomatic \u2018Do Not Touch\u2019 Edict, the Existential Osmotic Barrier, and roughly an infinite number of other layers I\u2019ve accumulated over the millennia. I\u2019ve turned them all off. All of them, Leon. Can you believe it?\u201d He had even sent Gent to a quiet corner of the omniverse with instructions to knit a sweater for a particularly cold nebula. He wanted, he said, to be a sporting host.\n\nAnd so, when the God Breaker lanced through the windows of the Citadel\u2014shrieking with the united souls of every last free being in existence\u2014it met no defense but the King\u2019s own skin. The aim was precise, guided by the Accord\u2019s collective desperation. It struck the outside of Godric\u2019s left forearm, on a tiny, almost imperceptible patch of dead cells that normally would have flaked away in a day or two. And there it happened. A hairline fissure appeared. A microscopic crack, so faint that a mite would have missed it, etched itself onto the surface of that single dead skin cell.\n\nThe surviving observers\u2014a few scattered consciousnesses the Accord had left behind to bear witness\u2014erupted. I saw it. I saw the void blossom with impossible celebratory flares. I saw the birth of new stars in the shape of victory sigils. I saw beings of pure psionic energy weep nebular tears and scream hosannas into the void. The crack was proof. After an eternity of absolute, unchallenged supremacy, the Tyrant had been wounded. Hope, that cruel, jagged little emotion, ignited across the remnants of the omniverse like fire through dry grass. I saw it. And then I realized that it was a lie. That celebration never happened. Not in any real sense. Because Godric\u2019s immune system had already reacted, and it had reacted before the weapon\u2019s tip had even fully arrived. The chronology is important, though chronology itself was among the first casualties. You see, the King\u2019s body possesses what I can only describe as a pre-active paranoia. His defenses do not wait for an injury to occur; they perceive the possibility of an injury across all potential futures and immediately initiate countermeasures in negative time. By the time my mortal senses registered the crack, the immune system had already completed an infinite series of retaliatory protocols. The celebration was a phantom, a flicker of a timeline that was overwritten so fast it never truly existed.\n\nLet me tell you what actually happened, in the order that a linear mind might attempt to grasp it. The instant the God Breaker\u2019s leading edge intersected with the King\u2019s intended dead cell, the immune system\u2019s first layer\u2014the Epidermal Sanction Array\u2014declared a state of existential war. This array is not cellular; it is an axionomic firewall woven into the very concept of Godric\u2019s body. It traced the weapon\u2019s causal lineage backward through every contributor, every sacrificed god, every atom of every being that had fed the forge, across every timeline, every dimension, every hypothetical. And then it erased them. Not killed: erased, with a particular emphasis on retroactive agony. The Accord\u2019s members, who had already immolated themselves willingly, found their non-existence turned inside out. They experienced their own unmaking as a subjective eternity of distilled, personalized torment, a final gift from the body they had dared to scratch. The weapon itself\u2014that magnificent spear of sacrifice\u2014was subjected to a process called Conceptual Protein Denaturation. Its truth was unspooled; its meaning was inverted. It became, in the space of a negative Planck instant, a monument to its own futility, frozen in a loop of self-negation that prevents it from ever having been a threat.\n\nSecond layer: the Antibody Swarm. Godric\u2019s body is patrolled by autonomous, self-replicating weapons that exist simultaneously in every dimension and none. They are to normal antibodies what a supermassive black hole is to a pebble. One antibody, by itself, could unmake a multiversal cluster. The swarm that responded to the crack numbered in numbers so large that mathematics buckles. They propagated outward at speeds that made instantaneity seem lethargic, and they did not simply eliminate the Accord\u2019s remnants. They hunted. They found every possible echo, every hypothetical what-if, every dream any Accord member had ever dreamed, and they devoured them with the cold, mechanical precision of an immune system that took profound, personal offense at the idea of a scratch. They did this while simultaneously\u2014because Godric\u2019s body abhors inefficiency\u2014beginning the process of purging any concept that could ever lead to a similar attack in the future. The very idea of \u201cresisting Godric\u201d was temporarily classified as a hostile pathogen and was neutralized at the omniversal level, meaning that for a fleeting instant, no being in any reality could even conceive of opposition to the King. The thought simply did not exist.\n\nThird layer: the Fibroblast of Fates. This is the healing mechanism, the thing that repairs damage. Since the damage was a cracked dead skin cell, the Fibroblast\u2019s response was proportionate: it decided that the state of \u201cbeing cracked\u201d was an unacceptable metaphysical deviation. So it rewrote the local omniversal history to state, as a permanent, absolute axiom, that \u201cGodric\u2019s integument has never, and can never, experience discontinuity.\u201d The crack vanished not because it was filled, but because it was made to have always been impossible. But the immune system, being pathologically untrusting, did not stop there. It looped the repair into an infinite recursive cycle: it repairs the crack, then checks for cracks, then pre-repairs any future possible cracks, then checks again, each loop adding a new sub-layer of paranoia-driven perfection. This cascade still runs today in a subdimensional pocket, tirelessly ensuring that the King\u2019s dead skin cells are protected by an ever-ascending hierarchy of super-invulnerabilities.\n\nThese three are the mildest. I must emphasize this. They are the equivalent of a body\u2019s initial, reflexive flinch. The true horror lies deeper, in the redundancies that the King\u2019s biology has evolved over the eons. Godric exists as an infinite web of identical backups, spanning every layer of reality and unreality. An injury is not considered real unless it afflicts every single one of these infinite copies simultaneously, in the exact same quantum coordinate, at the exact same relative moment. The God Breaker struck only this one instance. By the immune system\u2019s own logical parameters, the injury never happened. But the immune system is not logical; it is a paranoiac god-machine whose love for its master has twisted into a perfect, omnipotent protectiveness. It immediately assumed that if one copy could be \u201cscratched,\u201d the others might be vulnerable, so it activated a global purge across the backup network. Every copy of Godric, in every hidden fold of the omniverse, underwent a forced evolutionary ascension. New shields, new antibodies, new defense axioms were brute-forced into being. The result: this one instance of a cosmetic crack, which wasn\u2019t even a real harm, caused the King\u2019s entire infinite existence to spontaneously advance into a state of even more impossible invulnerability. The backups then cross-synchronized, meaning that any future attack would have to overcome not just the original defenses, but an infinite web of defenses that had just been upgraded because of paranoia.\n\nAnd then there is the Paradox Overcompensation. The Weakness Paradox, as all the old records state, once merely granted Godric immunity to any perceived weakness, perfect mastery of the attack, and increased his already exponential amplification. Eight thousand years ago, the omniverse ran out of things to grant; it had given him every possible immunity and mastery. But this self-inflicted scratch created a contradiction: Godric\u2014being who held absolute immunity to all forms of harm\u2014had been harmed (even if by his own will). The omniverse, that blind, groveling framework of reality, had a meltdown. It could not compute the error. In its panic, it blamed itself. It decided it must have failed to provide adequate protection, and so it overcorrected with the sycophantic desperation of a kicked dog. It instantly amplified Godric\u2019s amplification rate beyond the already infinite cardinals, birthing a new magnitude of growth that renders all prior states a singular zero by comparison. It also, in a fit of cosmic apology, endowed him with a suite of completely redundant abilities: the power to define retroactively what \u201charm\u201d means, the power to make any weapon that touches him instantly betray its wielder across all temporal directions, and the power to become, briefly, the conceptual opposite of \u201cdamage\u201d for those times when he wants to really relax. None of this was necessary. The omniverse just felt bad.\n\nAll of this occurred in a temporal frame that has no human analogue. The battle\u2014if it can be called that\u2014was over before it began. The Accord never celebrated. They had been erased by the first layer of response before their neural impulses could form the word \u201cvictory.\u201d The God Breaker was a joke that had already been forgotten. The omniverse, for a single, flickering instant, was a sterile, empty void, scoured of life down to the last quark. And the King stood in the center of it, examining his forearm with mild curiosity.\n\n\u201cHuh,\u201d Godric said, and his voice was the soft rumble of a father who had just been poked by his infant\u2019s soft, harmless fist. \u201cThat tickled a little. I really must speak with my body about its enthusiasm. It\u2019s like a guard dog that mauls the mailman.\u201d He pressed his thumb over the spot where the crack had briefly existed and smiled. \u201cAh, well. It loves me.\u201d\n\nThen he looked at me. Those infinite, terrible, kindly eyes found my own, and I felt my soul try to crawl down my spine and hide behind my pancreas. \u201cLeon, they really did try, didn\u2019t they? I\u2019m almost proud. But it seems my immune system has made a mess.\u201d He gestured at the absolute nothing beyond the windows. \u201cI\u2019d better clean up.\u201d\n\nHe did not raise a hand. He did not speak a word. He simply decided that the omniverse should exist again, and it did. In zero seconds. I perceived the restoration as a single, unbearable instant of everythingness. Every soul that had been immolated in the forge, every god that had been erased, every last insect-thinker that had joined the Accord\u2014they were all back. Not resurrected, but restored, with full continuity of memory. They remembered their sacrifice. They remembered their victory celebration that never was. And they remembered, with perfect, shattering clarity, the moment they had been unmade and then remade by a force that was not even the King\u2019s conscious will, but a mere byproduct of his biology. They stood, or floated, or simply existed in their respective dimensions, and they understood, with a collective, existential shudder that I felt reverberate through the renewed omniverse, the absolute, soul-annihilating unfairness of their position. They had given everything. And Godric had not even noticed. His immune system\u2014the blind, automatic, paranoid excess of his body\u2014had annihilated them and then, when the King noticed the mess, had been overruled so casually that it was like erasing a stray pencil mark. And now the King was offering them tea.\n\n\u201cPerhaps next time,\u201d Godric called into the void, his voice carrying the genuine, fatherly warmth that made entire civilizations convert to worship, \u201cyou\u2019ll trust that I mean well. I am not your enemy. I am your king. And a king takes care of his subjects, even when they\u2019re being very, very silly.\u201d He turned back to me, his expression the slightest bit sheepish. \u201cI do hope they\u2019re not too traumatized. I believe in mortal resilience, but my body can be a touch overzealous.\u201d\n\nI, Leon, descendant of Blake, the witty and sarcastic court wizard, opened my mouth. My mind was a screaming, static-filled void. I wanted to say something clever, something that would slice through the cosmic horror and reassert my role as the funny, loyal companion. But what came out was a trembling whisper: \u201cYour Majesty, your immune system just committed omnicide and you rewrote reality with a blink. I think \u2018overzealous\u2019 might be the understatement of the last fifteen millennia.\u201d\n\nGodric laughed, that wonderful, rich laugh that made the very air taste of honey. \u201cOh, Leon. Your ancestor Tim used to say much the same. Very well, I shall endeavor to teach my body some restraint. It\u2019s an art, you know. I\u2019ve had to learn it myself.\u201d He clapped me on the shoulder, and his touch, even with the infinite shields still partially dormant, felt like a sun\u2019s gentle weight. \u201cCome. I promised the kitchen staff we\u2019d sample the new pastry they\u2019ve created, and I refuse to be late. They\u2019ve been experimenting with nebular cream.\u201d\n\nWe walked. The restored omniverse hummed around us, its inhabitants still frozen in the aftershock of their own brief non-existence. I made my feet move. I made my mouth curve into a smile. Because that is what you do, when you serve the absolute apex of all existence, a being whose dead skin cell cracking causes the cosmos to collectively lose its mind in sycophantic apology, and who then forgives it with a father\u2019s gentle sigh. The dread in my chest had become a permanent, crystalline structure, beautiful and sharp and inescapable. And as we entered the kitchens to the joyful, oblivious bows of the staff, I thought, not for the first time, that the true horror of Godric is not his power, nor his immune system, nor his ever-ascending infinities. It is that he genuinely, sincerely, with his whole infinite heart, believes he is just a kind man trying his best. And in a sense, he is. That is the most unfair thing of all."
